<p>As of 2022, the top five manufacturers worldwide were Samsung (21%), Apple (16%), Xiaomi (13%), Oppo (10%), and Vivo (9%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>History</dt></dl>
<p>From 1983 to 1998, <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a> was market leader in mobile phones. <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> was the market leader in mobile phones from 1998 to 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In Q1 2012, <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> surpassed Nokia, selling 93.5 million units as against Nokia's 82.7 million units. Samsung has retained its top position since then. 
</p><p>Aside from Motorola, European brands such as Nokia, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a> once held large sway over the global mobile phone market, and many new technologies were pioneered in Europe. By 2010, the influence of European companies had significantly decreased due to fierce competition from American and Asian companies, to where most technical innovation had shifted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Apple and Google, both of the United States, also came to dominate mobile phone software.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_mobile_phone_operator">By mobile phone operator</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_operator" title="Mobile phone operator">Mobile phone operator</a></div><p>The world's largest individual mobile operator by number of subscribers is <a href="/wiki/China_Mobile" title="China Mobile">China Mobile</a>, which has over 902 million mobile phone subscribers as of June 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mobile_phone&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Over 50 mobile operators have over ten million subscribers each, and over 150 mobile operators had at least one million subscribers by the end of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In 2014, there were more than seven billion mobile phone subscribers worldwide, a number that is expected to keep growing.
</p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use">Use</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Smartphone#Use" title="Smartphone">Smartphone § Use</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="602" data-file-width="886" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg/350px-Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg/525px-Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg/700px-Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mobile_phone_subscribers_1997-2014_ITU.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mobile phone subscribers per 100 inhabitants. 2014 figure is estimated.</div></div></div>
<p>Mobile phones are used for a variety of purposes, such as keeping in touch with family members, for conducting business, and in order to have access to a telephone in the event of an emergency. Some people carry more than one mobile phone for different purposes, such as for business and personal use. Multiple SIM cards may be used to take advantage of the benefits of different calling plans.  For example, a particular plan might provide for cheaper local calls, long-distance calls, international calls, or roaming.
</p><p>The mobile phone has been used in a variety of diverse contexts in society.  For example:
</p>
<ul><li>A study by <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola</a> found that one in ten mobile phone subscribers have a second phone that is often kept secret from other family members. These phones may be used to engage in such activities as extramarital affairs or clandestine business dealings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li>Some organizations assist victims of domestic violence by providing mobile phones for use in emergencies. These are often refurbished phones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>The advent of widespread text-messaging has resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Cell_phone_novel" title="Cell phone novel">cell phone novel</a>, the first literary genre to emerge from the cellular age, via <a href="/wiki/Text_messaging" title="Text messaging">text messaging</a> to a website that collects the novels as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mobile_telephony" title="Mobile telephony">Mobile telephony</a> also facilitates activism and <a href="/wiki/Citizen_journalism" title="Citizen journalism">citizen journalism</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> reported that mobile phones have spread faster than any other form of technology and can improve the livelihood of the poorest people in developing countries, by providing access to information in places where <a href="/wiki/Landline" title="Landline">landlines</a> or the Internet are not available, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a>. Use of mobile phones also spawns a wealth of micro-enterprises, by providing such work as selling airtime on the streets and repairing or refurbishing handsets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> and other African countries, people used to travel from village to village to let friends and relatives know about weddings, births, and other events.  This can now be avoided in areas with mobile phone coverage, which are usually more extensive than areas with just land-line penetration.</li>
<li>The TV industry has recently started using mobile phones to drive live TV viewing through mobile apps, advertising, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_TV" title="Social TV">social TV</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_TV" title="Mobile TV">mobile TV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> It is estimated that 86% of Americans use their mobile phone while watching TV.</li>
<li>In some parts of the world, mobile phone sharing is common. Cell phone sharing is prevalent in urban India, as families and groups of friends often share one or more mobile phones among their members. There are obvious economic benefits, but often familial customs and traditional gender roles play a part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> It is common for a village to have access to only one mobile phone, perhaps owned by a teacher or missionary, which is available to all members of the village for necessary calls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_distribution">Content distribution</span></h3>
<p>In 1998, one of the first examples of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Content_distribution" title="Content distribution">distributing and selling media content</a> through the mobile phone was the sale of <a href="/wiki/Ringtone" title="Ringtone">ringtones</a> by <a href="/wiki/Radiolinja" title="Radiolinja">Radiolinja</a> in Finland. Soon afterwards, other media content appeared, such as news, video games, jokes, horoscopes, TV content and advertising. Most early content for mobile phones tended to be copies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legacy_media" title="Legacy media">legacy media</a>, such as banner advertisements or TV news highlight video clips. Recently, unique content for mobile phones has been emerging, from ringtones and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ringback_tones" title="Ringback tones">ringback tones</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobisodes" title="Mobisodes">mobisodes</a>, video content that has been produced exclusively for mobile phones.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_banking_and_payment">Mobile banking and payment</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mobile_payment_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="695" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Mobile_payment_01.jpg/220px-Mobile_payment_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Mobile_payment_01.jpg/330px-Mobile_payment_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Mobile_payment_01.jpg/440px-Mobile_payment_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mobile_payment_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mobile payment system</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mobile_banking" title="Mobile banking">Mobile banking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_payment" title="Mobile payment">Mobile payment</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branchless_banking" title="Branchless banking">Branchless banking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">Contactless payment</a></div>
<p>In many countries, mobile phones are used to provide <a href="/wiki/Mobile_banking" title="Mobile banking">mobile banking</a> services, which may include the ability to transfer cash payments by secure SMS text message. Kenya's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M-PESA" title="M-PESA">M-PESA</a> mobile banking service, for example, allows customers of the mobile phone operator <a href="/wiki/Safaricom" title="Safaricom">Safaricom</a> to hold cash balances which are recorded on their SIM cards. Cash can be deposited or withdrawn from M-PESA accounts at Safaricom retail outlets located throughout the country and can be transferred electronically from person to person and used to pay bills to companies.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branchless_banking" title="Branchless banking">Branchless banking</a> has also been successful in South Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. A pilot project in <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> was launched in 2011 by the <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> bank, <a href="/wiki/Bank_Mandiri" title="Bank Mandiri">Bank Mandiri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mobile payments were first trialled in Finland in 1998 when two Coca-Cola vending machines in <a href="/wiki/Espoo" title="Espoo">Espoo</a> were enabled to work with SMS payments. Eventually, the idea spread and in 1999, the Philippines launched the country's first commercial mobile payments systems with mobile operators <a href="/wiki/Globe_Telecom" title="Globe Telecom">Globe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smart_Communications" title="Smart Communications">Smart</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Some mobile phones can make <a href="/wiki/Mobile_payment" title="Mobile payment">mobile payments</a> via direct mobile billing schemes, or through <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">contactless payments</a> if the phone and the <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">point of sale</a> support <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near_field_communication" title="Near field communication">near field communication</a> (NFC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Enabling contactless payments through NFC-equipped mobile phones requires the co-operation of manufacturers, network operators, and retail merchants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_tracking">Mobile tracking</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cellphone_surveillance" title="Cellphone surveillance">Cellphone surveillance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_tracking" title="Mobile phone tracking">Mobile phone tracking</a></div>
<p>Mobile phones are commonly used to collect location data. While the phone is turned on, the geographical location of a mobile phone can be determined easily (whether it is being used or not) using a technique known as <a href="/wiki/Multilateration" title="Multilateration">multilateration</a> to calculate the differences in time for a signal to travel from the mobile phone to each of several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cell_towers" title="Cell towers">cell towers</a> near the owner of the phone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-phone-locate_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-phone-locate-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foxnews-phone-locate_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-phone-locate-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>The movements of a mobile phone user can be tracked by their service provider and, if desired, by law enforcement agencies and their governments. Both the <a href="/wiki/SIM_card" title="SIM card">SIM card</a> and the handset can be tracked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-phone-locate_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-phone-locate-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>China has proposed using this technology to track the commuting patterns of Beijing city residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>  In the UK and US, law enforcement and intelligence services use mobile phones to perform surveillance operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roving-bugs_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-roving-bugs-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hackers have been able to track a phone's location, read messages, and record calls, through obtaining a subscribers phone number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="While_driving">While driving</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phones_and_driving_safety" title="Mobile phones and driving safety">Mobile phones and driving safety</a> and <a href="/wiki/Texting_while_driving" title="Texting while driving">Texting while driving</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG/220px-Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG/330px-Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG/440px-Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hand_held_phone_in_car.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A driver using two handheld mobile phones at once</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG/220px-NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG/330px-NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG/440px-NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NocellphonesSouthsidePlaceTX.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A sign in the U.S. restricting cell phone use to certain times of day (no cell phone use between 7:30am-9:00am and 2:00pm-4:15pm)</div></div></div>
<p>Mobile phone use while driving, including talking on the phone, texting, or operating other phone features, is common but controversial. It is widely considered dangerous due to <a href="/wiki/Distracted_driving" title="Distracted driving">distracted driving</a>. Being distracted while operating a motor vehicle has been shown to increase the risk of accidents. In September 2010, the US <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) reported that 995 people were killed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restrictions_on_cell_phone_use_by_U.S._drivers" title="Restrictions on cell phone use by U.S. drivers">drivers distracted by cell phones</a>. In March 2011, a U.S. insurance company, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Farm_Insurance" title="State Farm Insurance">State Farm Insurance</a>, announced the results of a study which showed 19% of drivers surveyed accessed the Internet on a smartphone while driving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-65">[65]</a></sup> Many jurisdictions prohibit the use of mobile phones while driving. In Egypt, Israel, Japan, Portugal, and Singapore, both handheld and hands-free use of a mobile phone (which uses a <a href="/wiki/Speakerphone" title="Speakerphone">speakerphone</a>) is banned.  In other countries, including the UK and France and in many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restrictions_on_cell_phone_use_by_US_drivers" title="Restrictions on cell phone use by US drivers">U.S. states</a>, only handheld phone use is banned while hands-free use is permitted.
</p><p>A 2011 study reported that over 90% of college students surveyed text (initiate, reply or read) while driving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
The scientific literature on the dangers of driving while sending a text message from a mobile phone, or <i><a href="/wiki/Texting_while_driving" title="Texting while driving">texting while driving</a></i>, is limited. A simulation study at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah" title="University of Utah">University of Utah</a> found a sixfold increase in distraction-related accidents when texting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the increasing complexity of mobile phones, they are often more like mobile computers in their available uses. This has introduced additional difficulties for law enforcement officials when attempting to distinguish one usage from another in drivers using their devices. This is more apparent in countries which ban both handheld and hands-free usage, rather than those which ban handheld use only, as officials cannot easily tell which function of the mobile phone is being used simply by looking at the driver. This can lead to drivers being stopped for using their device illegally for a phone call when, in fact, they were using the device legally, for example, when using the phone's incorporated controls for car stereo, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">GPS</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satnav" title="Satnav">satnav</a>.
</p><p>A 2010 study reviewed the incidence of mobile phone use while <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> and its effects on behaviour and safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In 2013, a national survey in the US reported the number of drivers who reported using their cellphones to access the Internet while driving had risen to nearly one of four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> A study conducted by the University of Vienna examined approaches for reducing inappropriate and problematic use of mobile phones, such as using mobile phones while driving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>Accidents involving a driver being distracted by talking on a mobile phone have begun to be prosecuted as negligence similar to speeding. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, from 27 February 2007, motorists who are caught using a hand-held mobile phone while driving will have three penalty points added to their license in addition to the fine of £60.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-71">[71]</a></sup> This increase was introduced to try to stem the increase in drivers ignoring the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC2_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> prohibits all mobile phone use while driving, including use of hands-free devices.  New Zealand has banned hand-held cell phone use since 1 November 2009. Many states in the United States have banned texting on cell phones while driving. Illinois became the 17th American state to enforce this law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-73">[73]</a></sup> As of July 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mobile_phone&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 30 states had banned texting while driving, with Kentucky becoming the most recent addition on 15 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courier-Journal_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Courier-Journal-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Public_health_law" title="Public health law">Public Health Law Research</a> maintains a list of distracted driving laws in the United States. This database of laws provides a comprehensive view of the provisions of laws that restrict the use of mobile communication devices while driving for all 50 states and the District of Columbia between 1992 when first law was passed, through 1 December 2010. The dataset contains information on 22 dichotomous, continuous or <a href="/wiki/Categorical_variable" title="Categorical variable">categorical variables</a> including, for example, activities regulated (e.g., texting versus talking, hands-free versus handheld), targeted populations, and exemptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, an estimated 1500 pedestrians were injured in the US while using a cellphone and some jurisdictions have attempted to ban pedestrians from using their cellphones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">Health effects</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_radiation_and_health" title="Mobile phone radiation and health">Mobile phone radiation and health</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nomophobia" title="Nomophobia">Nomophobia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_overuse" title="Mobile phone overuse">Mobile phone overuse</a></div>
<p>The effect of mobile phone radiation on human health is the subject of recent<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> interest and study, as a result of the enormous increase in mobile phone usage throughout the world. Mobile phones use <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">electromagnetic radiation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Microwave" title="Microwave">microwave</a> range, which some believe may be harmful to human health. A large body of research exists, both <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">epidemiological</a> and experimental, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_model" title="Animal model">non-human animals</a> and in humans.  The majority of this research shows no definite causative relationship between exposure to mobile phones and harmful biological effects in humans. This is often paraphrased simply as the balance of evidence showing no harm to humans from mobile phones, although a significant number of individual studies do suggest such a relationship, or are inconclusive. Other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wireless_electronic_devices_and_health" title="Wireless electronic devices and health">digital wireless systems</a>, such as data communication networks, produce similar radiation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>On 31 May 2011, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> stated that mobile phone use may possibly represent a long-term health risk,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Health_Organization_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Health_Organization-79">[79]</a></sup> classifying mobile phone radiation as "possibly carcinogenic to humans" after a team of scientists reviewed studies on mobile phone safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnnwhocarcinogenic_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnnwhocarcinogenic-80">[80]</a></sup> The mobile phone is in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_IARC_Group_2B_carcinogens" title="List of IARC Group 2B carcinogens">category 2B</a>, which ranks it alongside <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> and other possibly carcinogenic substances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some recent<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> studies have found an association between mobile phone use and certain kinds of brain and salivary gland tumors. <a href="/wiki/Lennart_Hardell" title="Lennart Hardell">Lennart Hardell</a> and other authors of a 2009 meta-analysis of 11 studies from peer-reviewed journals concluded that cell phone usage for at least ten years "approximately doubles the risk of being diagnosed with a brain tumor on the same ('ipsilateral') side of the head as that preferred for cell phone use".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>One study of past mobile phone use cited in the report showed a "40% increased risk for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gliomas" title="Gliomas">gliomas</a> (brain cancer) in the highest category of heavy users (reported average: 30 minutes per day over a 10‐year period)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> This is a reversal of the study's prior position that cancer was unlikely to be caused by cellular phones or their base stations and that reviews had found no convincing evidence for other health effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Health_Organization_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_Health_Organization-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> However, a study published 24 March 2012, in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Medical_Journal" title="British Medical Journal">British Medical Journal</a></i> questioned these estimates because the increase in brain cancers has not paralleled the increase in mobile phone use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Certain countries, including France, have warned against the use of mobile phones by minors in particular, due to health risk uncertainties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Mobile pollution by transmitting electromagnetic waves can be decreased up to 90% by adopting the circuit as designed in mobile phone and mobile exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016, preliminary findings of a long-term study by the U.S. government suggested that radio-frequency (RF) radiation, the type emitted by cell phones, can cause cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_impact">Educational impact</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_use_in_schools" title="Mobile phone use in schools">Mobile phone use in schools</a></div>
<p>A study by the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics</a> found that banning mobile phones in schools could increase pupils' academic performance, providing benefits equal to one extra week of schooling per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_waste_regulation">Electronic waste regulation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg/220px-Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg/330px-Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg/440px-Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Handy_schrott_mobile_phone_scrap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scrapped mobile phones</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_recycling" title="Mobile phone recycling">Mobile phone recycling</a></div>
<p>Studies have shown that around 40–50% of the environmental impact of mobile phones occurs during the manufacture of their printed wiring boards and integrated circuits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>The average user replaces their mobile phone every 11 to 18 months,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and the discarded phones then contribute to <a href="/wiki/Electronic_waste" title="Electronic waste">electronic waste</a>.  Mobile phone manufacturers within <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> are subject to the <a href="/wiki/Waste_Electrical_and_Electronic_Equipment_Directive" title="Waste Electrical and Electronic Equipment Directive">WEEE directive</a>, and Australia has introduced a mobile phone recycling scheme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> had an advanced robotic disassembler and sorter called Liam specifically for recycling outdated or broken iPhones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theft">Theft</span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a>, one out of three robberies involve the theft of a cellular phone.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Police data in San Francisco show that half of all robberies in 2012 were thefts of cellular phones.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> An online petition on <a href="/wiki/Change.org" title="Change.org">Change.org</a>, called <i>Secure our Smartphones</i>, urged smartphone manufacturers to install <a href="/wiki/Kill_switch" title="Kill switch">kill switches</a> in their devices to make them unusable if stolen. The petition is part of a joint effort by New York Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schneiderman" title="Eric Schneiderman">Eric Schneiderman</a> and San Francisco District Attorney <a href="/wiki/George_Gasc%C3%B3n" title="George Gascón">George Gascón</a> and was directed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO">CEOs</a> of the major smartphone manufacturers and telecommunication carriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> On 10 June 2013, Apple announced that it would install a "<a href="/wiki/Kill_switch" title="Kill switch">kill switch</a>" on its <a href="/wiki/IOS_7" title="IOS 7">next iPhone operating system</a>, due to debut in October 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>All mobile phones have a unique identifier called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Mobile_Station_Equipment_Identity" title="International Mobile Station Equipment Identity">IMEI</a>. Anyone can report their phone as lost or stolen with their Telecom Carrier, and the IMEI would be blacklisted with a central registry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Telecom carriers, depending upon local regulation can or must implement blocking of blacklisted phones in their network. There are, however, a number of ways to circumvent a blacklist. One method is to send the phone to a country where the telecom carriers are not required to implement the blacklisting and sell it there,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> another involves altering the phone's IMEI number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Even so, mobile phones typically have less value on the second-hand market if the phones original IMEI is blacklisted.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_minerals">Conflict minerals</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_minerals" title="Conflict minerals">Conflict minerals</a></div>
<p>Demand for metals used in mobile phones and other electronics fuelled the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a>, which claimed almost 5.5 million lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In a 2012 news story, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> reported: "In unsafe mines deep underground in eastern Congo, <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">children are working</a> to extract minerals essential for the electronics industry. The profits from the minerals finance the bloodiest conflict since the second world war; the war has lasted nearly 20 years and has recently flared up again. For the last 15 years, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> has been a major source of natural resources for the mobile phone industry."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The company <a href="/wiki/Fairphone" title="Fairphone">Fairphone</a> has worked to develop a mobile phone that does not contain <a href="/wiki/Conflict_resource" title="Conflict resource">conflict minerals</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kosher_phones"><span class="anchor" id="Kosher_phone"></span>Kosher phones</span></h3>
<p>Due to concerns by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Jewish" title="Orthodox Jewish">Orthodox Jewish</a> rabbinate in Britain that texting by youths could waste time and lead to "immodest" communication, the rabbinate recommended that phones with text-messaging capability not be used by children; to address this, they gave their official approval to a brand of "Kosher" phones with no texting capabilities.  Although these phones are intended to prevent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immodesty#Judaism" title="Immodesty">immodesty</a>, some vendors report good sales to adults who prefer the simplicity of the devices; other Orthodox Jews question the need for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Israel, similar phones to kosher phones with restricted features exist to observe the <a href="/wiki/Shabbat" title="Shabbat">sabbath</a>; under Orthodox Judaism, the use of any electrical device is generally prohibited during this time, other than to save lives, or reduce the risk of death or similar needs. Such phones are approved for use by essential workers, such as health, security, and public service workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kosher_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-kosher-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
